title Why does this website exist? | justus.ws https://www.justus.ws/why/ 0
para It’s a mild allergic reaction to social media. It’s a place to put things I care about. It’s a place to experiment and have fun. It’s a place where I don’t have to worry about likes or whether one or 100 people are looking at what I’m putting out there. It’s in the tradition of putting time into creating a personal website as a creative expression. Remember GeoCities? It’s a modern GeoCities site. It’s Web 1.0. It’s a personal website. The personal website—once abundant and never quite endangered but certainly threatened—is making a comeback. This is my corner of the internet. https://www.justus.ws/why/ 0

para “Ever since I was 3, I’ve drawn and written out plans and dreams. Pencils, crayons, paints, paper, and notebooks have felt like an appendage most of my life. Since then, a large part of my work and passion has been attempting to make technology more useful, humane, and beautiful. But, I’ve always felt that there’s an immense gap between the freedom of a pen and paper and the powerful, but restrictive, nature of keystrokes and screens. Drawing on paper became a therapeutic escape into a different way of thinking. But all the while, I hoped that one day, the digital technology would catch up to the personal, free-from analog tech of pen and notebook. I doubted it would, though. A couple of years ago, I used my iPad Pro & Apple Pencil for the first time and felt that same therapeutic escape feeling while drawing in Procreate on a screen. Ever since then, my iPad is my constant companion for shifting between freeform, unencumbered drawing & scribbling and deeply linked, indexed writing. It’s not nearly as good as it could be yet, but it’s my favorite thing not only because it’s close enough, but also because it’s the first time I felt that the line between technical and humane mediums isn’t a real line at all.” https://www.justus.ws/misc/housewarming-gifts/paul-johnson/ 0

title s 3 3 d s https://fee.cool/sunday-sites/ephemeral/ 0
para Plants like to be together. Look at any forest, overgrown yard, prairie, or jungle. Green is everywhere. An ecology is a community, always changing, ephemeral. Moving always towards stability and dynamic health. Weeds pop up in the garden because your vegetables are lonely. When you plant something tall, like Corn, you will have vining weeds that crawl up the stalk. You will have wide, low weeds, which cover the ground between the Corn. Pulling and cutting these weeds takes a lot of work. Companion planting is a way to fill those niches with fruits and vegetables before the weeds sneak in. Many plants have reliable companionships with other plants, mutually beneficial relationships that grow together and leave no room for unwelcome invaders. Perhaps the best-known companion guild is the Three Sisters. https://fee.cool/sunday-sites/ephemeral/ 0

title The ultimate fruit fly trap | justus.ws https://www.justus.ws/food/fruit-fly-trap/ 0
para To make the most effective DIY fruit fly trap, use a hammer and a small nail to poke a few tiny holes in the lid of a Mason jar. Put a little bit of some sort of sweet vinegar in the jar. Apple Cider vinegar is the gold standard, but I’ve used sweet rice wine vinegar with good results as well (I also added a bit of honey to sweeten the deal). Add a drop of dish soap to break the surface tension and facilitate the drowning of the fruit flies. https://www.justus.ws/food/fruit-fly-trap/ 0

title Paul's iPad | justus.ws https://www.justus.ws/misc/housewarming-gifts/paul-johnson/ 0
para “Ever since I was 3, I’ve drawn and written out plans and dreams. Pencils, crayons, paints, paper, and notebooks have felt like an appendage most of my life. At six, I used my parent’s old typewriter to write out plans and scripts and illustrated around the margins. I also fell in love with computers in early high school, especially designing and creating with them. Since then, a large part of my work and passion has been attempting to make technology more useful, humane, and beautiful. But, I’ve always felt that there’s an immense gap between the freedom of a pen and paper and the powerful, but restrictive, nature of keystrokes and screens. Drawing on paper became a therapeutic escape into a different way of thinking. But all the while, I hoped that one day, the digital technology would catch up to the personal, free-from analog tech of pen and notebook. I doubted it would, though. A couple of years ago, I used my iPad Pro & Apple Pencil for the first time and felt that same therapeutic escape feeling while drawing in Procreate on a screen. Ever since then, my iPad is my constant companion for shifting between freeform, unencumbered drawing & scribbling and deeply linked, indexed writing. It’s not nearly as good as it could be yet, but it’s my favorite thing not only because it’s close enough, but also because it’s the first time I felt that the line between technical and humane mediums isn’t a real line at all.” https://www.justus.ws/misc/housewarming-gifts/paul-johnson/ 0
